Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. Normalize to ValidationError and let its constructor\n            # do the hard work of making sense of the input.\n            error = ValidationError(error)\n\n        if hasattr(error, \"error_dict\"):\n            if field is not None:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    \"The argument `field` must be `None` when the `error` \"\n                    \"argument is a dictionary.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                error = error.error_dict\n        else:\n            error = {field or NON_FIELD_ERRORS: error.error_list}\n\n        for field, error_list in error.items():\n            if field not in self.errors:\n                if field != NON_FIELD_ERRORS and field not in self.fields:\n                    raise ValueError(\n                        \"'%s' has no field named '%s'.\"\n                        % (self.__class__.__name__, field)\n                    )\n                if field == NON_FIELD_ERRORS:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer\n                    )\n                else:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        renderer=self.renderer,\n                        field_id=self[field].auto_id,\n                    )\n            self._errors[field].extend(error_list)\n            if field in self.cleaned_data:\n                del self.cleaned_data[field]\n\n    def has_error(self, field, code=None):\n        return field in self.errors and (\n            code is None\n            or any(error.code == code for error in self.errors.as_data()[field])\n        )","numLines":60,"startLine":264,"totalLines":443}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01H4YWLsPnkqDPf6gsWqQLuw","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01XwiLnJ1STsp3g2Q7X7pNJr","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/COMPOSITE_VALIDATOR_EXAMPLE.md","content":"# CompositeFieldValidator Usage Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nThe `CompositeFieldValidator` class allows you to validate relationships between multiple form fields. This is useful for validations that depend on the values of more than one field, such as:\n\n- Ensuring an end date is after a start date\n- Confirming that a password and password confirmation match\n- Validating that an email address matches a confirmed email address\n- Any other multi-field validation logic\n\n## Basic Usage\n\n### 1. Define a Validation Function\n\nFirst, create a validation function that takes `cleaned_data` as an argument and raises `ValidationError` if validation fails:\n\n```python\nfrom django.core.exceptions import ValidationError\n\ndef validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Validate that end_date is after start_date.\"\"\"\n    start_date = cleaned_data.get('start_date')\n    end_date = cleaned_data.get('end_date')\n\n    if start_date and end_date and end_date <= start_date:\n        raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date.\")\n```\n\n### 2. Attach the Validator to Your Form\n\nUse the `CompositeFieldValidator` as a class attribute on your form:\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom django.forms import CompositeFieldValidator\n\nclass EventForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            validate_date_range,\n            ['start_date', 'end_date'],\n            'Invalid date range'  # Optional error message\n        )\n    ]\n```\n\n## Advanced Usage\n\n### Multiple Composite Validators\n\nYou can attach multiple validators to the same form:\n\n```python\ndef validate_dates(cleaned_data):\n    # ... validation logic\n\ndef validate_capacity(cleaned_data):\n    # ... validation logic\n\nclass EventForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n    expected_attendees = forms.IntegerField()\n    venue_capacity = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_dates, ['start_date', 'end_date']),\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_capacity, ['expected_attendees', 'venue_capacity']),\n    ]\n```\n\n### Field-Specific Error Messages\n\nTo add errors to specific fields:\n\n```python\ndef validate_password_match(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Validate that password fields match.\"\"\"\n    password = cleaned_data.get('password')\n    password_confirm = cleaned_data.get('password_confirm')\n\n    if password and password_confirm and password != password_confirm:\n        # This error will be attached to the 'password' field\n        raise ValidationError(\"Passwords do not match.\")\n\nclass RegistrationForm(forms.Form):\n    password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    password_confirm = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            validate_password_match,\n            ['password', 'password_confirm']\n        )\n    ]\n```\n\n### Dictionary-Based Error Handling\n\nFor more complex validation with errors on multiple fields:\n\n```python\ndef validate_form_data(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Complex validation with multiple field errors.\"\"\"\n    errors = {}\n\n    if some_condition(cleaned_data):\n        errors['field1'] = \"Error message for field1\"\n\n    if another_condition(cleaned_data):\n        errors['field2'] = \"Error message for field2\"\n\n    if errors:\n        raise ValidationError(errors)\n\nclass ComplexForm(forms.Form):\n    field1 = forms.CharField()\n    field2 = forms.CharField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_form_data, ['field1', 'field2'])\n    ]\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### What Happens If a Field Doesn't Exist?\n\nIf you reference a field that doesn't exist on the form, a `ValueError` will be raised during form validation:\n\n```python\nclass MyForm(forms.Form):\n    field1 = forms.CharField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            lambda cd: None,\n            ['field1', 'nonexistent_field']  # This will cause an error\n        )\n    ]\n\nform = MyForm({'field1': 'value'})\nform.full_clean()  # Raises: ValueError: Field 'nonexistent_field' does not exist on form 'MyForm'.\n```\n\n### How Errors Are Attached\n\nWhen a `ValidationError` is raised from the validation function:\n\n1. If the error has a dictionary of field-specific errors, they are attached to their respective fields\n2. Otherwise, the error is attached to the **first field** in the `field_names` list\n\n## Integration with Django's Validation Pipeline\n\nThe `CompositeFieldValidator` integrates seamlessly with Django's form validation:\n\n1. `Form.full_clean()` is called\n2. `_clean_fields()` - All individual field validators run\n3. `_clean_form()` - The form's `clean()` method runs\n4. `_post_clean()` - **Composite validators run here**\n\nThis ensures that:\n- Individual field validation happens first\n- Custom form-level validation (`clean()`) method still works\n- Composite validators have access to all cleaned field values\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Keep Validators Pure**: Validators should not modify form state; they should only validate data\n2. **Use Descriptive Names**: Choose clear names for your validation functions\n3. **Document Complex Logic**: Add docstrings to complex validation functions\n4. **Handle Missing Values**: Check for None/empty values before comparing fields\n5. **Use Appropriate Error Messages**: Provide clear error messages that help users understand what went wrong\n\n## Example: Complete Form\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom bounds.\"\"\"\n    min_age = cleaned_data.get('min_age')\n    max_age = cleaned_data.get('max_age')\n\n    if min_age and max_age and min_age > max_age:\n        raise ValidationError(\"Minimum age start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_age_range, ['min_age', 'max_age']),\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_dates, ['start_date', 'end_date']),\n    ]\n```\n\n## Testing\n\nWhen testing forms with composite validators:\n\n```python\nfrom django.test import TestCase\n\nclass This is useful for validations that depend on the values of more than one field, such as:\n\n- Ensuring an end date is after a start date\n- Confirming that a password and password confirmation match\n- Validating that an email address matches a confirmed email address\n- Any other multi-field validation logic\n\n## Basic Usage\n\n### 1. Define a Validation Function\n\nFirst, create a validation function that takes `cleaned_data` as an argument and raises `ValidationError` if validation fails:\n\n```python\nfrom django.core.exceptions import ValidationError\n\ndef validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Validate that end_date is after start_date.\"\"\"\n    start_date = cleaned_data.get('start_date')\n    end_date = cleaned_data.get('end_date')\n\n    if start_date and end_date and end_date <= start_date:\n        raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date.\")\n```\n\n### 2. Attach the Validator to Your Form\n\nUse the `CompositeFieldValidator` as a class attribute on your form:\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom django.forms import CompositeFieldValidator\n\nclass EventForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            validate_date_range,\n            ['start_date', 'end_date'],\n            'Invalid date range'  # Optional error message\n        )\n    ]\n```\n\n## Advanced Usage\n\n### Multiple Composite Validators\n\nYou can attach multiple validators to the same form:\n\n```python\ndef validate_dates(cleaned_data):\n    # ... validation logic\n\ndef validate_capacity(cleaned_data):\n    # ... validation logic\n\nclass EventForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n    expected_attendees = forms.IntegerField()\n    venue_capacity = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_dates, ['start_date', 'end_date']),\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_capacity, ['expected_attendees', 'venue_capacity']),\n    ]\n```\n\n### Field-Specific Error Messages\n\nTo add errors to specific fields:\n\n```python\ndef validate_password_match(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Validate that password fields match.\"\"\"\n    password = cleaned_data.get('password')\n    password_confirm = cleaned_data.get('password_confirm')\n\n    if password and password_confirm and password != password_confirm:\n        # This error will be attached to the 'password' field\n        raise ValidationError(\"Passwords do not match.\")\n\nclass RegistrationForm(forms.Form):\n    password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    password_confirm = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            validate_password_match,\n            ['password', 'password_confirm']\n        )\n    ]\n```\n\n### Dictionary-Based Error Handling\n\nFor more complex validation with errors on multiple fields:\n\n```python\ndef validate_form_data(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Complex validation with multiple field errors.\"\"\"\n    errors = {}\n\n    if some_condition(cleaned_data):\n        errors['field1'] = \"Error message for field1\"\n\n    if another_condition(cleaned_data):\n        errors['field2'] = \"Error message for field2\"\n\n    if errors:\n        raise ValidationError(errors)\n\nclass ComplexForm(forms.Form):\n    field1 = forms.CharField()\n    field2 = forms.CharField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(validate_form_data, ['field1', 'field2'])\n    ]\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### What Happens If a Field Doesn't Exist?\n\nIf you reference a field that doesn't exist on the form, a `ValueError` will be raised during form validation:\n\n```python\nclass MyForm(forms.Form):\n    field1 = forms.CharField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            lambda cd: None,\n            ['field1', 'nonexistent_field']  # This will cause an error\n        )\n    ]\n\nform = MyForm({'field1': 'value'})\nform.full_clean()  # Raises: ValueError: Field 'nonexistent_field' does not exist on form 'MyForm'.\n```\n\n### How Errors Are Attached\n\nWhen a `ValidationError` is raised from the validation function:\n\n1. If the error has a dictionary of field-specific errors, they are attached to their respective fields\n2. Otherwise, the error is attached to the **first field** in the `field_names` list\n\n## Integration with Django's Validation Pipeline\n\nThe `CompositeFieldValidator` integrates seamlessly with Django's form validation:\n\n1. `Form.full_clean()` is called\n2. `_clean_fields()` - All individual field validators run\n3. `_clean_form()` - The form's `clean()` method runs\n4. `_post_clean()` - **Composite validators run here**\n\nThis ensures that:\n- Individual field validation happens first\n- Custom form-level validation (`clean()`) method still works\n- Composite validators have access to all cleaned field values\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Keep Validators Pure**: Validators should not modify form state; they should only validate data\n2. **Use Descriptive Names**: Choose clear names for your validation functions\n3. **Document Complex Logic**: Add docstrings to complex validation functions\n4. **Handle Missing Values**: Check for None/empty values before comparing Used for model validation in model forms.\n       \"\"\"\n       # Run composite validators if present\n       for validator in getattr(self, 'composite_validators', []):\n           validator(self)\n   ```\n\n**Why `_post_clean()`?**\n- Called after all field-level cleaning and the `clean()` method\n- Guarantees `cleaned_data` contains all validated values\n- Errors can be properly added to the form\n- Maintains backward compatibility with existing code\n\n### 3. `/workspace/django/forms/__init__.py` (MODIFIED)\n**Change Made**:\n```python\nfrom django.forms.validators import CompositeFieldValidator  # NOQA\n```\n\nExports the `CompositeFieldValidator` class so it can be imported directly from `django.forms`.\n\n## Features Implemented\n\n✅ **CompositeFieldValidator class exists** in Django's forms package\n✅ **Integrates with form validation pipeline** through `_post_clean()` method\n✅ **Uses Django's validation error classes** (ValidationError)\n✅ **Handles missing field references gracefully** (raises ValueError with clear message)\n✅ **Valid Python syntax** (verified with py_compile)\n✅ **Changes scoped to django/forms/** (no changes to other packages)\n✅ **Can be used as class attribute** on form definitions\n✅ **Supports multiple validators** on a single form\n✅ **Supports dict-based error distribution** to multiple fields\n\n## Usage Example\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom django.core.exceptions import ValidationError\nfrom django.forms import CompositeFieldValidator\n\ndef validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n    \"\"\"Ensure end_date is after start_date.\"\"\"\n    start_date = cleaned_data.get('start_date')\n    end_date = cleaned_data.get('end_date')\n\n    if start_date and end_date and end_date <= start_date:\n        raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date.\")\n\nclass EventForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n    composite_validators = [\n        CompositeFieldValidator(\n            validate_date_range,\n            ['start_date', 'end_date'],\n            'Invalid date range'\n        )\n    ]\n```\n\n## How It Works\n\n1. Developer defines a validation function that takes `cleaned_data` as argument\n2. Developer creates a form with a `composite_validators` list containing `CompositeFieldValidator` instances\n3. When `form.is_valid()` is called:\n   - `full_clean()` runs the normal validation pipeline\n   - Individual field validators run\n   - `clean()` method runs\n   - `_post_clean()` runs, which executes all composite validators\n4. Validators check conditions across fields and raise `ValidationError` if validation fails\n5. Errors are attached to appropriate fields using `form.add_error()`\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Missing Field References\nIf a validator references a field that doesn't exist:\n```\nValueError: Field 'nonexistent' does not exist on form 'MyForm'.\n```\n\n### Validation Errors\n- **Simple errors**: Attached to the first field in `field_names`\n- **Dict-based errors**: Distributed to their respective fields\n- **Non-field errors**: Can be raised with `field=None`\n\n## Integration Points\n\n### With Custom clean() Method\nThe form's custom `clean()` method continues to work:\n- `clean()` runs before composite validators\n- Both can coexist without conflicts\n\n### With Field-Level Validators\nField-level validators run first, then:\n- `clean()` method\n- Composite validators\n\n### Inheritance\nComposite validators work with form inheritance:\n```python\nclass BaseForm(forms.Form):\n    composite_validators = [validator1]\n\nclass DerivedForm(BaseForm):\n    composite_validators = [validator1, validator2]  # Includes inherited validators\n```\n\n## Design Decisions\n\n1. **Class Attribute vs Metaclass**: Used class attribute approach (like fields) for simplicity\n2. **Execution Order**: Placed in `_post_clean()` to ensure all cleaned_data is available\n3. **Error Attachment**: First field approach provides reasonable default behavior\n4. **Callable Pattern**: Follows Django's validator pattern (callable classes)\n5. **@deconstructible**: Allows use in migrations\n\n## Testing\n\nComprehensive test suite in `/workspace/tests/forms_tests/tests/test_composite_validator.py` covers:\n- Basic instantiation and attributes\n- Validator execution and failure\n- Error attachment to correct fields\n- Multiple validators on single form\n- Missing field reference handling\n- Dict-based error distribution\n- Optional field handling\n- Integration with custom `clean()` method\n\n## Documentation\n\n- **COMPOSITE_VALIDATOR_EXAMPLE.md**: Detailed usage guide with examples\n- **Docstrings**: Comprehensive docstrings in validator class and methods\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\n✅ No breaking changes - adds optional functionality\n✅ Existing forms continue to work unchanged\n✅ Default `composite_validators = []` means no performance impact if not used\n\n## Performance\n\n✅ Minimal overhead - just iterates list of validators in `_post_clean()`\n✅ No changes to hot paths in form validation\n✅ Validators are user-defined, so performance depends on validator logic\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":177,"cache_read_input_tokens":63326,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":177},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a29ef0e4-7ddb-43cd-8d3a-9559d4aa5c7c","uuid":"2cb65693-41cb-433e-9490-71a7e97439d9"}

When `form.is_valid()` is called:\n   - `full_clean()` runs the normal validation pipeline\n   - Individual field validators run\n   - `clean()` method runs\n   - `_post_clean()` runs, which executes all composite validators\n4. Errors are attached to appropriate fields using `form.add_error()`\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Missing Field References\nIf a validator references a field that doesn't exist:\n```\nValueError: Field 'nonexistent' does not exist on form 'MyForm'.\n```\n\n### Validation Errors\n- **Simple errors**: Attached to the first field in `field_names`\n- **Dict-based errors**: Distributed to their respective fields\n- **Non-field errors**: Can be raised with `field=None`\n\n## Integration Points\n\n### With Custom clean() Method\nThe form's custom `clean()` method continues to work:\n- `clean()` runs before composite validators\n- Both can coexist without conflicts\n\n### With Field-Level Validators\nField-level validators run first, then:\n- `clean()` method\n- Composite validators\n\n### Inheritance\nComposite validators work with form inheritance:\n```python\nclass BaseForm(forms.Form):\n    composite_validators = [validator1]\n\nclass DerivedForm(BaseForm):\n    composite_validators = [validator1, validator2]  # Includes inherited validators\n```\n\n## Design Decisions\n\n1. **Class Attribute vs Metaclass**: Used class attribute approach (like fields) for simplicity\n2. **Execution Order**: Placed in `_post_clean()` to ensure all cleaned_data is available\n3. **Error Attachment**: First field approach provides reasonable default behavior\n4. **Callable Pattern**: Follows Django's validator pattern (callable classes)\n5. **@deconstructible**: Allows use in migrations\n\n## Testing\n\nComprehensive test suite in `/workspace/tests/forms_tests/tests/test_composite_validator.py` covers:\n- Basic instantiation and attributes\n- Validator execution and failure\n- Error attachment to correct fields\n- Multiple validators on single form\n- Missing field reference handling\n- Dict-based error distribution\n- Optional field handling\n- Integration with custom `clean()` method\n\n## Documentation\n\n- **COMPOSITE_VALIDATOR_EXAMPLE.md**: Detailed usage guide with examples\n- **Docstrings**: Comprehensive docstrings in validator class and methods\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\n✅ No breaking changes - adds optional functionality\n✅ Existing forms continue to work unchanged\n✅ Default `composite_validators = []` means no performance impact if not used\n\n## Performance\n\n✅ Minimal overhead - just iterates list of validators in `_post_clean()`\n✅ No changes to hot paths in form validation\n✅ Validators are user-defined, so performance depends on validator logic\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
